  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer14903697148417023541">Ruin wakes up on Earth knowing only one thing: to Judge and Execute.<br/><br/>As an Angel of Judgment with no memory of his origins and no ability to communicate, he seeks help from Isadore, the first human he comes into contact with. Without realizing, he binds molecularity with the OCD Neuroscientist, and slowly becomes permanently attached to her.<br/><br/>But, there is a mission he's sent</span>
  <span id="freeText14903697148417023541" style="display:none">Ruin wakes up on Earth knowing only one thing: to Judge and Execute.<br /><br />As an Angel of Judgment with no memory of his origins and no ability to communicate, he seeks help from Isadore, the first human he comes into contact with. Without realizing, he binds molecularity with the OCD Neuroscientist, and slowly becomes permanently attached to her.<br /><br />But, there is a mission he's sent to accomplish and it isn't about Isadore. Or is it? Something about the eccentric and beautiful woman seems to be preventing him from remembering what he must do in order to complete his task on Earth. <br /><br />In the breathtaking third book of the Ruin Series, The Judgment, Ruin tackles missions designed to bring him face to face with the answers he desperately needs. Soon, however, he discovers that the clues he gains to unravel the mysteries of his mission will declare war on his heart and soul.</span>

<div id="review_1123116596" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1123116596" />
    <a title="Carol Heisz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22522204-carol-heisz"><img alt="Carol Heisz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528550520p2/22522204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1123116596?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol Heisz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol Heisz" href="/user/show/22522204-carol-heisz">Carol Heisz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1123116596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13564000003038267502">I don't usually read paranormal romance, but picked up this series because I like the author's other books. I've found, the further I get into the series, the better the books get. BUT, there are typos (I lost track of the number of times you're was used in place of your), missing details, wrong names, editorial issues - it feels like the book is being rushed into publication. While I like the characters and the storyline - I find these sorts of things to be at the top of my pet peeve list. If y</span>
  <span id="freeText13564000003038267502" style="display:none">I don't usually read paranormal romance, but picked up this series because I like the author's other books. I've found, the further I get into the series, the better the books get. BUT, there are typos (I lost track of the number of times you're was used in place of your), missing details, wrong names, editorial issues - it feels like the book is being rushed into publication. While I like the characters and the storyline - I find these sorts of things to be at the top of my pet peeve list. If you can see your way past these things, read the series - I'm going to buy the 4th book because I need to know how Ruin and Isadore cope with what's going on...</span>
  <a data-text-id="13564000003038267502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It’s all captured in screenshots that are going viral in the book community. I seems this author not only wants to dominate in the bedroom but in all places in his life and gets off on attacking people who don’t worship him. Unfortunately for him the Internet never forgets. I would not touch his books with a 100 ft pole to save my life. <br /><br />You can check facebook and twitter for proof. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1208567791579072649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1213531828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1213531828" />
    <a title="Valerie The Valkyrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30068066-valerie-the-valkyrie"><img alt="Valerie The Valkyrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401151576p2/30068066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1213531828?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie The Valkyrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie The Valkyrie" href="/user/show/30068066-valerie-the-valkyrie">Valerie The Valkyrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1213531828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10543882165205754844"><strong>Meh</strong><br/><br/>Soooooo... I've been reading this "Ruin" series by Lucian Bane. You know the one..., the "ineffable Dom"? What evs (rolls eyes). This guy who is supposedly a real life Dom-cum-Erotica-writer (and fyi, I'm talking the Latin word cum as in dual role, not the OTHER cum that he writes about, seemingly, incessantly).<br/><br/>Anyway, I won't judge his entire writing career nor his personal beliefs based on this one series, but there is def something weird that's kinda wigging me out about this dude and his </span>
  <span id="freeText10543882165205754844" style="display:none"><strong>Meh</strong><br /><br />Soooooo... I've been reading this "Ruin" series by Lucian Bane. You know the one..., the "ineffable Dom"? What evs (rolls eyes). This guy who is supposedly a real life Dom-cum-Erotica-writer (and fyi, I'm talking the Latin word cum as in dual role, not the OTHER cum that he writes about, seemingly, incessantly).<br /><br />Anyway, I won't judge his entire writing career nor his personal beliefs based on this one series, but there is def something weird that's kinda wigging me out about this dude and his writing. <br /><br />Maybe it's the off-putting duality of his writing, putting God and Finger-Fucking (or insert nearly any other erotic act here) in the same paragraph while insinuating that one is somehow linked to or acceptable within the same set of beliefs. I can't explain it. It's weird. Here I'll try:<br /><br />It's like the whole concept of Genesis 2:24 &amp; 25 <br />"Therefore shall a man leave his father and his mother, and shall cleave unto his wife: and they shall be one flesh.<br /><br />And they were both naked, the man and his wife, and were not ashamed."<br /><br />And Matthew 19:5 &amp; 6<br />" And said, For this cause shall a man leave father and mother, and shall cleave to his wife: and they twain shall be one flesh? <br /><br />Wherefore they are no more twain, but one flesh. What therefore God hath joined together, let not man put asunder."<br /><br />(Side note, I don't know if my Grandmother would be proud or ashamed of my Bible recall in this instance...)<br /><br />It's like these passages were the basis for his justification of inserting religion into my erotica reading. Thanks, but no thanks. I don't want to think that while the hero is giving the protagonist the best head of her life and she's moaning, "Oh, God... Oh, God, YES!!" that God is actually listening and looking down with an affable, fatherly expression going, "Very nice, this is exactly what I meant by cleaving...carry on youngsters." Especially when the two aren't legally married in a church. <br /><br />Oh, I know, it's erotica...and I'm not being a Mary Sue, here (I've read Ann Rice's Sleeping Beauty trilogy, and any lingering Mary Sue thoughts or tendencies were permanently seared, through my corneas, from my psyche, forever and ever. Amen)..Anyway, I'm not trying to be prudish but if you're going to put God and Religion as the basis for your moral foundation and bring Him up repeatedly, I need you to be married for me to believe that God condones the extramarital porn hijnks these two are up to. And the dude (spoiler alert) is an Angel??!! Def need a priest here, stat.<br /><br />Anyway, the heroine (and I use that term verrra loosely to describe the female protagonist), is annoying as fuck. If she were real life, I'd probably set her on fire because she's that super stupid. Her stupidity literally fills volumes. I hate her more with every passing page. Her stupid should have a cape with an emblem and a bat signal. It's that super. The hero (who actually isn't that terribly written of a character) had my pity through out all three and a half books I've read today. I'm FORCING myself to finish the 4th and final volume just because I need to see if this female has any redeeming value.<br /><br />Jesus, this author either wants me to hate her and is a genius (although, I can't see what purpose that would serve in the story arc..., I think I'm supposed to like her or at least feel sorry for her?)... or he so poorly understands women IRL, that he should just jump to M/M Christian erotica and never, EVER write another female character EVER... EVER!!!! NEVER, ever!!!<br /><br />The story itself is pretty interesting,I guess. I didn't hate it. Kind of Armageddon, End Of Days prophesy shit with Angels and Demons and Grim Reaper and what not.. it's not terrible conceptually. <br /><br />I'm kind of in Love with one of the side characters, Scriber, who should get his own series where the author co-writes with someone who knows how to write a fucking woman's POV, and I'd read that shit all day long.<br /><br />But the "thing" that's, I think, most annoying to me about this author is, I get this feeling that he thinks that he's imparting some vast knowledge and secret wisdom about God and Carnality to his readers through this story and that it's meant to be allegorical, to be deciphered for a deeper meaning and to challenge your precepts of good and evil or something. Look dude, Mr LUCIAN BANE, Dante Alighier you are NOT... and this is certainly not his Inferno. Get over yourself.<br /><br />Anyway, 2.5 stars...would have given it 3.5 if not for the "heroine". Read at the risk of your sanity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10543882165205754844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3710758316389696745" style="display:none"><b>Judgement: Never easy and always heartbreaking. </b><br /><br />Once again Lucian Bane, the master of words has continued to torture and lead his readers on a pathway to utter despondency. The relationship between Ruin and Isadore continues to grow. Acknowledgement of emotions is a huge one in this, the third instalment of this superbly written series. Heartbreaking at times, funny, dramatic and definitely HOT, Ruin: The Judgement will leave you with more questions than answers. But that is the beauty of this story, it draws you, makes you become one with the characters - only an exceptional writer has the ability to work this type of magic and Lucian Bane does it every time he types a word.<br /><br />Deeply thought provoking and amazingly emotional, this is a series definitely not to be missed.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yZf/y4nEKl01eVs4KCl2OXFYTypbBi4VfJxXX2IeYsiVpj+SJsYIZA88mnOP9OcwON/sz6xEYTtS0NFgaHm2JA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZUNSf80MNM/n91bu9I+ucYcNevvLLn589GAS7ofojrw5cpImYg4W9t2yl6VTUj94zorZHjxsMVLaLJTRjY9aUA==')})
  }
